  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_138c8e8c-09d0-431e-a677-0783463d422f'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

  <span id="freeText9521422149914271872" style="display:none">One hundred very short chapters, told in an utterly original first-person voice, propel readers through a narrative that is by turns gripping and darkly humorous, bleak and chilling, tender and transporting.<br /><br />What if the football hadn't gone over the wall. On the other side of the wall there is a dark secret. And the devil. And the Moon Man. And the Motherland doesn't want anyone to know. But Standish Treadwell - who has different-colored eyes, who can't read, can't write, Standish Treadwell isn't bright - sees things differently than the rest of the "train-track thinkers." So when Standish and his only friend and neighbor, Hector, make their way to the other side of the wall, they see what the Motherland has been hiding. And it's big...</span>

<div id="review_1665132338" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1665132338" />
    <a title="Murf the Surf" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47868173-murf-the-surf"><img alt="Murf the Surf" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1445226640p2/47868173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1665132338?book_show_action=true">Jun 10, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Murf the Surf" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Murf the Surf" href="/user/show/47868173-murf-the-surf">Murf the Surf</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18308900-maggot-moon">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1665132338" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14065954442428251873">This could possibly be my very first review on GRs. I hope that many of you understand my predicament by now: I've been quite caught up in the alternate universe of Amazon. Thus, this is where at least two hundred of my previous reviews are stored. I've found the GR community to be quite forgiving and generous to a fault. I love you all so much for putting up with my non sensical diatribes about not finding the review button on my glow kindle. Mark Monday was one of the first to enlighten me and</span>
  <span id="freeText14065954442428251873" style="display:none">This could possibly be my very first review on GRs. I hope that many of you understand my predicament by now: I've been quite caught up in the alternate universe of Amazon. Thus, this is where at least two hundred of my previous reviews are stored. I've found the GR community to be quite forgiving and generous to a fault. I love you all so much for putting up with my non sensical diatribes about not finding the review button on my glow kindle. Mark Monday was one of the first to enlighten me and be friends. God bless you Mark. Many soon came to my aid, and here is a first time review experience.<br /> Now, to get to the book! I feel so many mixed emotions about Stanlish and his beloved grandfather. It is all he has, you see, as his parents were brutally taken from him along with everyone else. It is an alternate universe, like I'd described earlier for me, in 1957, in a sort of right wing fascist state. The author Sally Gardner know how to propel properly a pregnant pause, akin to a great comedian's comic pause. We don't know exactly where or what we are in the beginning, however quickly siding with Standish. They do meet another family and he makes a friend. I'm really afraid of revealing too much here, but will tell you this: much of what we dream of and want in life, is of our own imagination, creating a reality of it's own.<br /> Please look for this book at your local library and or download a digital copy. I've suffered great loss and pain in my own personal life. I don't wish to unload it all on this site. I was in a coma for four month and woke up paralyzed you see. Like Standish, we mustn't take each other or our families for granted. I'll consider writing my own tome about it someday. Maggot Moon showed me that our genetics show up who we SHOULD be related to by way of family, town, district or country. However, our real families are our own creation you see. Standish will show you the way. Like he, me and you, we'll all have our illustrious epiphany someday. And, I dearly hope that day coming is not too late.<br /> Please let me know how you've liked my first review on GRs, Murf</span>
  <a data-text-id="14065954442428251873" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_977501892" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/977501892" />
    <a title="Lisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32532774-lisa"><img alt="Lisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480492067p2/32532774.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/977501892?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa" href="/user/show/32532774-lisa">Lisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781471400445" href="/book/show/17246383-maggot-moon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32532774-lisa?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/32532774-lisa?shelf=carnegie-medal-and-shortlist">carnegie-medal-and-shortlist</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer977501892" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12572735576067177714">This story is as disturbing as it is multi-faceted.<br/><br/>Set in an alternative 1950s past in a dystopian England after World War II, reigned by a totalitarian regime which seems to follow a mixture of Stalinist and Nazi dogma, it tells the story of a young boy called Standish Treadwell. <br/><br/>Starting out as a bleak school boy story, featuring dyslexia and bullying issues, along with teacher abuse and authoritarian methods of teaching, it slowly reveals darker, and more dangerous elements, challenging the r</span>
  <span id="freeText12572735576067177714" style="display:none">This story is as disturbing as it is multi-faceted.<br /><br />Set in an alternative 1950s past in a dystopian England after World War II, reigned by a totalitarian regime which seems to follow a mixture of Stalinist and Nazi dogma, it tells the story of a young boy called Standish Treadwell. <br /><br />Starting out as a bleak school boy story, featuring dyslexia and bullying issues, along with teacher abuse and authoritarian methods of teaching, it slowly reveals darker, and more dangerous elements, challenging the reader to double-check the easily flowing language. Did the teacher just beat a student TO DEATH? Is that what the text says?<br /><br />Bits and pieces of propaganda make an appearance, a meta plot is taking shape: there are good and evil forces at work, the Motherland and its invisible, secret enemies. To prove eternal superiority, the Motherland is about to land a scientific coup: the first moon landing, years before enemy states are ready. That, the propaganda tells the citizens of the Motherland, will make it all-powerful. But Standish and his family happen to come across the horrible truth: it is all a hoax, and people are working on a fake show, only to be killed afterwards to avoid dangerous witnesses.<br /><br />In a political landscape of absolutely no hope at all, Standish decides to make a difference, to spoil the show, to hold up a sign in full view of the cameras of the world, to tell the world about the hoax. Knowing full well from experience that torture and death are the definitive consequences ...<br /><br />If you think this sounds harsh for a young adult novel, it is actually even more brutal than this. For in addition to the adventure and thrill of the action, there are pitiless philosophical questions built into the story line, starting with the sad introduction, Standish's thought experiment of turning back time to a point before his drama unfolded:<br /><br />"I'm wondering what if.<br />What if the football hadn't gone over the wall.<br />What if Hector had never gone looking for it.<br />What if he hadn't kept the dark secret to himself.<br />What if...<br />Then I suppose I would be telling myself another story.<br />You see, the what ifs are as boundless as the stars."<br /><br />For the reader, the list of moments when Standish could have been saved is incredibly painful. But at the same time, it is a story of the infinite number of choices you have, even in an oppressive, abusive environment. It is a story of the value of family, of love, of human dignity, as symbolised in Standish's old grandfather:<br /><br />"He stood tall and proud, always told me he owned nothing but his dignity and he wasn't about to give that away to no one. To no creed, to no church, to no dogma."<br /><br />It is a story telling us about the horrific effectiveness of terror, and the threat it poses to human dignity, first introduced when Standish's grandfather kills rats in the cellar, later to be shown with young boys as victims, parents as hostages:<br /><br />"Seven dead rats was something the king of rats would respect. Shoot one rat and all his relatives will come looking for you; shoot seven and they understand you mean business."<br /><br />The rats are a disgusting element of the society in decay, but they also are part of a sub plot told only in pictures, in a comic strip at the bottom of each page, slowly unfolding a truth of a different kind, giving subtle clues to the title of the book. It shows the curiosity of a rat, sniffing out a bottle that human beings immediately recognise as poisonous, reading the sign with the skull. It is an analogy to the optimistic, curious scientist experimenting without knowledge of the dangerous political environment he moves in. An accident ("What if...") makes the bottle tip over, and the rat poisons itself. What follows over hundreds of pages is a graphic illustration of the death and decomposition of the rat, until it is completely taken over by maggots and disappears. A fly hatches from a maggot and indicates a new life form, similar to the old one, but with new possibilities in store: What if... <br /><br />There is not only despair in that reflection, there is hope as well. What if one action made all the difference?<br /><br />When Standish sacrifices his life to make a difference for the future, he sums it up:<br /><br />"This is my moment. Not even one minute, just a moment. But maybe all it needs is a moment to change the course of history. I am on the moon. I am the stone. The plug is pulled on the maggot moon."<br /><br />What if you you read this book...<br />What if it makes you see things clearly...<br />What if it causes you pain and reading pleasure...<br />What if it makes you hope and despair...<br />What if it makes you imagine that one boy, one moment, one act can make a difference...<br /><br />It might be worthwhile.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12572735576067177714" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Stacey (prettybooks)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3533262-stacey-prettybooks"><img alt="Stacey (prettybooks)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577577052p2/3533262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/358602420?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacey (prettybooks)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacey (prettybooks)" href="/user/show/3533262-stacey-prettybooks">Stacey (prettybooks)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781471400049" href="/book/show/14060279-maggot-moon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=read-in-my-twenties">read-in-my-twenties</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=read-after-university">read-after-university</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=young-adult-fiction">young-adult-fiction</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer358602420" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1639347639396769054">Imagine living in an alternative universe, but one eerily similar to Nazi Germany. Is this historical fantasy? Historical science fiction? It's like nothing I've read before, but that's the thrill of it. Standish Treadwell and his grandfather – Gramps – live in Zone Seven, where outcasts and political anarchists are sent. They have nothing except some scraps of food to get them through the winter and contraband television. We all know about Nazi Germany. But do the citizens in <em>Maggot Moon</em> fare t</span>
  <span id="freeText1639347639396769054" style="display:none">Imagine living in an alternative universe, but one eerily similar to Nazi Germany. Is this historical fantasy? Historical science fiction? It's like nothing I've read before, but that's the thrill of it. Standish Treadwell and his grandfather – Gramps – live in Zone Seven, where outcasts and political anarchists are sent. They have nothing except some scraps of food to get them through the winter and contraband television. We all know about Nazi Germany. But do the citizens in <em>Maggot Moon</em> fare the same?<br /><br /><em>Maggot Moon</em> is an example of compelling, inventive and truly great storytelling. Although some chapters are only a mere half a page, by the end of the book you've become immersed in Standish's world, and genuinely understand what he has gone through. And what he goes through is horrific. It's a book you'll finish the same day you pick it up. There is no need for overly long and detailed descriptions – Standish lives in a brutal, harsh place where people are blinded by propaganda. There's no time for lyrics and poetry.<br /><br />You see, Standish also has dyslexia, meaning that people underestimate him. (It also doesn't help that he has one brown eye and one blue eye!). He's intelligent yet perceived to have the mind of a young child, so he's constantly running from bullies – students and teachers alike. And then there's the soldiers – Greenflies – who are the eyes and ears of those at the top of the social ladder, making sure that everybody sticks to the rules. It's set in bleak 1956 where the Motherland want to demonstrate ultimate supremacy and be the first nation to land on the moon. But Standish and Gramps have an inkling that something is not quite right, and are determined to reveal the truth.<br /><br />Narrated by a unique voice and with a host of characters you cannot help but fight for, the brilliantly haunting and highly compelling <em>Maggot Moon</em>, winner of the 2012 Costa Children's Book Award, is definitely one you won't want to miss!<br /><br /><i>Thank you Hot Key Books for providing this book for review!</i><br /><br /><i>I also reviewed this book over on <a href="http://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/book-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pretty Books</a>.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="1639347639396769054" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_722123436" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/722123436" />
    <a title="Sally Whitehead" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5874718-sally-whitehead"><img alt="Sally Whitehead" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1327850444p2/5874718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/722123436?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sally Whitehead" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sally Whitehead" href="/user/show/5874718-sally-whitehead">Sally Whitehead</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781471400049" href="/book/show/14060279-maggot-moon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5874718-sally-whitehead?shelf=books-read-in-2013">books-read-in-2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer722123436" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16775073219451012702">Quite simply, I did not GET this book. I don't get the hype and rave reviews it has received, but more significantly I don't get WHO it was written for or what it's trying to say or achieve.<br/><br/>I was expecting it to be a good crossover text, written for young adults, but very much easily enjoyed and appreciated by adult readers alike. Not so. If this was written for young adults, it's WAY off the mark in my opinion. I teach teenagers - I WANT books to be written for them which will challenge them an</span>
  <span id="freeText16775073219451012702" style="display:none">Quite simply, I did not GET this book. I don't get the hype and rave reviews it has received, but more significantly I don't get WHO it was written for or what it's trying to say or achieve.<br /><br />I was expecting it to be a good crossover text, written for young adults, but very much easily enjoyed and appreciated by adult readers alike. Not so. If this was written for young adults, it's WAY off the mark in my opinion. I teach teenagers - I WANT books to be written for them which will challenge them and open their minds, but I fail to see how "Maggot Moon" hopes to do this. Historical allegory? Maybe so, but novels such as "Boy in the Striped Pyjamas" do that far better. Maybe I simply prefer realism?<br /><br />It's not the disturbing subject matter which grates if the intended audience is young adults, it's the clumsiness of it - the sudden introduction of profanities towards the end, the brief (as in one paragraph) foray into homosexuality...it's just all over the place, and thus impossible to take seriously - if that's what it wants?<br /><br />One of the most jarring things as a reader was the occasional glitch in spelling or incorrect use of words...at first I thought this was an editorial error, but then after a few times realised it must be intentional. I understand the narrator is dyslexic, and this is probably supposed to demonstrate this, but for me this simply didn't work. To go from "the proganda-perfect face paint" to the word "propoganda" (and far more complex words) being spelt perfectly throughout the rest of the novel is just irritating. 130 pages later we get "the figures I saw last night march pass us" - stylistically it's not consistent enough for it to take effect. Similarly towards the end Standish has a Mrs Malaprop moment when he says "It's quite a rigor mortis to place it exactly at the right spot", presumably meaning "rigmarole" - again, if consistently used this could be an effective device. It isn't.<br /><br />But, plenty of people are loving this book, so maybe it's just me and I am completely missing something.<br /><br />Very disappointing.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16775073219451012702" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2044518418" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2044518418" />
    <a title="Praxedes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4413597-praxedes"><img alt="Praxedes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291464885p2/4413597.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2044518418?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Praxedes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Praxedes" href="/user/show/4413597-praxedes">Praxedes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2044518418" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10396026247457030309">Thanks to Goodreads member Ellen Lee for recommending this delightful book. Set in a dystopian past reminiscent of Nazi-era Germany, this story chronicles the slow disintegration of a family by a totalitarian regime.<br/><br/>At first read the tale seemed simplistic, but over the course of the novel I was able to become engrossed in it. The book also features an interesting graphic vignette of other creatures associated with despair such as flies and rats.<br/><br/>Highly recommended for Young Adults.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_699546310" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/699546310" />
    <a title="Jack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8604196-jack"><img alt="Jack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541189436p2/8604196.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/699546310?book_show_action=true">Aug 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jack" href="/user/show/8604196-jack">Jack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781471400445" href="/book/show/17246383-maggot-moon">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer699546310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10677417423929332238">Introduced in 1939, The Carnegie Medal is perhaps the most prestigious of children’s/YA book awards, with any winner (or even shortlisted title) gaining a bank account buckling sales boost. The latest winner (2013) is Maggot Moon by Sally Gardener, a dystopian fable which follows dyslexic protagonist, Standish Tredwell.<br/><br/>Standish lives in a kind of alternate realty in which the ‘Motherland’ has taken control of 1950’s England. Surveillance, disappearances and capital punishment are the daily norm,</span>
  <span id="freeText10677417423929332238" style="display:none">Introduced in 1939, The Carnegie Medal is perhaps the most prestigious of children’s/YA book awards, with any winner (or even shortlisted title) gaining a bank account buckling sales boost. The latest winner (2013) is Maggot Moon by Sally Gardener, a dystopian fable which follows dyslexic protagonist, Standish Tredwell.<br /><br />Standish lives in a kind of alternate realty in which the ‘Motherland’ has taken control of 1950’s England. Surveillance, disappearances and capital punishment are the daily norm, and the rat-infested streets are virtually an inhabitable ruin. It’s a pretty grim existence and Standish’s dyslexia, fierce imagination, as well as his one blue and one brown eye, make him a prime target for the regime and it’s hierarchy of violent bullies.<br /><br />Fending off starvation thanks to a couple of hens and a meagre vegetable patch, Standish lives with his Gramps in a modest Zone 7 house not far from his brutish school. His parents have been taken by the regime, and he and his grandfather tread the fine line between surviving and subverting their totalitarian oppressors. However, a secret hidden below Standish’s house could hold the key to toppling the Motherland. That, or certain death of course.<br /><br />Maggot Moon is presented in one hundred concise chapters and the writing, particularly the use of metaphor, is stunning – one particular sentence describes Standish’s beating heart as ‘an egg bumping against the side of a pan of boiling water’. Throughout the novel, Gardner’s pros are deceptively simplistic and, in many ways, bear more than a passing resemblance to 2012’s Carnegie winner, A Monster Calls by Patrick Ness.<br /><br />In Standish’s world, the only person he can call a friend him is newcomer to Zone 7, Hector. Even though the pair forge a strong bond, and friendship in the face of adversity is an important theme here, this is no fairy tale and the conclusion has serious emotional clout. A worthy winner indeed.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10677417423929332238" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_596300965" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/596300965" />
    <a title="Hayley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4517828-hayley"><img alt="Hayley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305069934p2/4517828.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hayley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hayley" href="/user/show/4517828-hayley">Hayley</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4517828-hayley?shelf=sciencefiction">sciencefiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4517828-hayley?shelf=survival">survival</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4517828-hayley?shelf=realistic">realistic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4517828-hayley?shelf=highschool">highschool</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4517828-hayley?shelf=tragedy">tragedy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4517828-hayley?shelf=middleschool">middleschool</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4517828-hayley?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4517828-hayley?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4517828-hayley?shelf=disability">disability</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer596300965" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4188560868659244846">What an amazing read! I re-read this as soon as I'd finished it - first time I've ever done that. This is like reading '1984' narrated by Christopher from 'The Curious Incident...' It is set in a 1956 in which the Nazis won the war (this is not explicitly stated, but the clues are there, I think) and Standish and his grandfather live in Zone Seven - where the 'impure' are sent. Standish is dyslexic (maybe, again never stated explicitly) and it is his use of language that makes this such an incre</span>
  <span id="freeText4188560868659244846" style="display:none">What an amazing read! I re-read this as soon as I'd finished it - first time I've ever done that. This is like reading '1984' narrated by Christopher from 'The Curious Incident...' It is set in a 1956 in which the Nazis won the war (this is not explicitly stated, but the clues are there, I think) and Standish and his grandfather live in Zone Seven - where the 'impure' are sent. Standish is dyslexic (maybe, again never stated explicitly) and it is his use of language that makes this such an incredible read - he is not a 'train track thinker' and twists everyday adages which creates startling new images ("a hare's breath" for example). The story is rooted in Standish's friendship with Hector, which is so beautifully evoked that the ending is unbearably sad. The illustrations of rats, flies and maggots baffled me at first, but on the second reading I could see how they run as a harmony to the prose, as well as personifying (if that's what it is with an animal) the corruption, decay and rot at the heart of the Motherland. This is a really short book (100 chapters, some of which are only a paragraph long) and deceptively simple, but as the author does not spell everything out for the reader it is a densely rich,intense and rewarding read. (Just as a caution, there is some brutal violence which is made worse by the apparent everyday casualness of its occurrence - it is not Hollywood movie violence but is imaginably real)</span>
  <a data-text-id="4188560868659244846" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alice Oseman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alice Oseman" href="/user/show/11436874-alice-oseman">Alice Oseman</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1017342421" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6236843398259279384">I originally bought this book for my younger brother, thinking it might get him into reading as it has very short chapters and a cool cover. He didn't read it, because he hates to read books. So I thought I'd give it a go instead.<br/><br/>Maggot Moon reminded me of The Book Thief, except it's one billion times better (and I adore The Book Thief). It's on an entirely different playing field. I think the main thing that makes it so amazing is its startling originality. But I can't fault anything about this</span>
  <span id="freeText6236843398259279384" style="display:none">I originally bought this book for my younger brother, thinking it might get him into reading as it has very short chapters and a cool cover. He didn't read it, because he hates to read books. So I thought I'd give it a go instead.<br /><br />Maggot Moon reminded me of The Book Thief, except it's one billion times better (and I adore The Book Thief). It's on an entirely different playing field. I think the main thing that makes it so amazing is its startling originality. But I can't fault anything about this book. <br /><br />I've never read a dystopian book like it. It manages to confront this particular world without needing to explain at any point what has happened - this is what makes the book so wonderfully abstract. The language is utterly beautiful, the characters and relationships are heartbreaking, and the story manages to cross genres and themes and create something so filmic and powerful that you are not going to forget about it for a very long time.<br /><br />This book deserves every prize it has won. Whatever sort of a reader you are, you need to read it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6236843398259279384" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3601195367836275148">OH bloody hell!!! <br/>Okay, I chose to read this book because everyone was talking about it saying it was a really good and short alternative history set in 1950s Britain. I assumed it was a middle grade book, which is not, and I also assumed it was not going to be as dark as it truly was.   <span id="freeText3601195367836275148" style="display:none">OH bloody hell!!! <br />Okay, I chose to read this book because everyone was talking about it saying it was a really good and short alternative history set in 1950s Britain. I assumed it was a middle grade book, which is not, and I also assumed it was not going to be as dark as it truly was. The writing was beautiful, Standish Treadwell is not very smart, but he has an ample vocabulary that makes me suck in the text and I will definitely be dreaming about it tonight. The language was so soft that it made me worry about the characters (which in this genre I know not to do), and the world building did not feel rushed or non-existent, which is a problem with short books. <br />And that little twist at the end, I thought about it, but I suspected they were not going to put it there, but it was such a nice move to rip off my heart in the end. Great book, highly recommend. </span>

<div id="review_596108730" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/596108730" />
    <a title="Louise / Daisy May Johnson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5230131-louise-daisy-may-johnson"><img alt="Louise / Daisy May Johnson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554735943p2/5230131.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/596108730?book_show_action=true">Apr 21, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Louise / Daisy May Johnson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Louise / Daisy May Johnson" href="/user/show/5230131-louise-daisy-may-johnson">Louise / Daisy May Johnson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781471400049" href="/book/show/14060279-maggot-moon">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer596108730" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12963989583231144680">There's a difficulty for me in reviewing this, and one that I hope to address through the act of reviewing. I admit that's a fairly Moebius-esque sentence but I hope that it becomes clearer the further I go on.<br/><br/>Gardner's superb. Her writing here is very beautiful, very stunning and occasionally cut from the clearest of glass which shines a little more every time you look at it. But, when I reflect on it, and when that reflection takes days to formulate clearly, I think I realise something. I real</span>
  <span id="freeText12963989583231144680" style="display:none">There's a difficulty for me in reviewing this, and one that I hope to address through the act of reviewing. I admit that's a fairly Moebius-esque sentence but I hope that it becomes clearer the further I go on.<br /><br />Gardner's superb. Her writing here is very beautiful, very stunning and occasionally cut from the clearest of glass which shines a little more every time you look at it. But, when I reflect on it, and when that reflection takes days to formulate clearly, I think I realise something. I realise that I don't think I like this book.<br /><br />There's nothing wrong with that. Every book has readers who will fall in love and readers who will collapse in horror at the first sentence, but what I do have my issues with is when people do this and don't interrogate themselves as to why. And thus, this is my interrogation.<br /><br />There were elements of this book that I loved; the narrative, spiderwebbing together, pulling images and text and breathless moments of silence into the spiralling bravery and madness of Standish Treadwell. Structurally, it's brilliant. Short, tight chapters that fade in and out of consciousness, borderline poetic in their brevity and conciseness. <br /><br />But I think the crux of my curious disconnect with this book as a whole, is the fact that I felt that when it came to it, I didn't matter. That's a selfish point of view for a reader to admit to, but I think it's a vital one to realise. I want to matter to my books, to make some sort of a difference, to actualise and catalyse them, and I don't think I ever felt like I did matter with Maggot Moon.<br /><br />That's all well and good, but what I do acknowledge is that as a conceptual whole, this book is brilliant. It's doing things that I admire, wholly, and I can admire that. I can admire Gardner's intense, brave, lyrical prose. I can admire the brilliant addition of the picture based narrative, paralleling the main story as a whole, adding a layer of subtle emphasis to the narrative and the reading experience. I can admire all that and I can admit that.<br /><br />But I don't think I can admit that I liked it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12963989583231144680" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1307693303" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17195068592376289238">Book #2 of MLI2015<br/>(A book from the genre I read the least last year)<br/><br/>What an amazing story!<br/>If the title isn't enough to grip you in and make you want to pick up the book instantly, consider this:<br/><br/>Standish Treadwell has one eye each colour and besides not being very literate, he is one of the smartest in his class. Motherland emprisions him. His only friend is his Grandfather who he is living with because his parents have disappeared without a trace, as so many other people do - wiped out completel</span>
  <span id="freeText17195068592376289238" style="display:none">Book #2 of MLI2015<br />(A book from the genre I read the least last year)<br /><br />What an amazing story!<br />If the title isn't enough to grip you in and make you want to pick up the book instantly, consider this:<br /><br />Standish Treadwell has one eye each colour and besides not being very literate, he is one of the smartest in his class. Motherland emprisions him. His only friend is his Grandfather who he is living with because his parents have disappeared without a trace, as so many other people do - wiped out completely, without any warning or explaination. Standish says dying and disappearing must be the same thing, because all of them leave a void. In his cellar he is hiding a Moon Man. His only friend Hector is not here anymore.<br /><br />Dwell with my in this amazing plotline and you will not be disappointed. Characters are built well, the atmosphere in itself makes up for a good picture, but there's no overdescription. There's enough mystery to keep you turning the pages until you can't do it anymore. In all honesty, I finished this book in one sitting and it took me no time at all.<br />It is a sad story, indeed, and I do recommend tissues. The last pages gave me goosebumps. It is a strange thing when you give yourself away completely to what you're reading. I did and I do not regret it.<br />Chapters are short enough, which makes you keep up a pace and keep on turning pages.<br /><br />It is, overall, a really well-written book about friendship, loyalty, and being the outcast. It isn't perfect, but it will warm you up inside. I highly recommend.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer518303344" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer14242930346047956130">2.5<br/><br/>While I liked the book, it underwhelmed me. I didn't become invested in any of the characters. I had a hard time connecting to them, Standish and his friends are supposed to be 15 years old, but the entire story read like he was 10 years old, not to mention the cover. There were words like 'hell' and 'shi*' and even an 'f' bomb or two that would indicate that it was perhaps an older teen read but the story and characters didn't read that way. <br/><br/>I also felt as if it were anti-climactic. While Sa</span>
  <span id="freeText14242930346047956130" style="display:none">2.5<br /><br />While I liked the book, it underwhelmed me. I didn't become invested in any of the characters. I had a hard time connecting to them, Standish and his friends are supposed to be 15 years old, but the entire story read like he was 10 years old, not to mention the cover. There were words like 'hell' and 'shi*' and even an 'f' bomb or two that would indicate that it was perhaps an older teen read but the story and characters didn't read that way. <br /><br />I also felt as if it were anti-climactic. While Sally Gardner did a nice job of creating a different kind of world through her word imaging, the 'thing' over the wall just didn't feel as big as it was supposed to be. </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer722821729" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17299966413629407489">I really wanted to like this novel, and truthfully it wasn't all bad. It just wasn't good either. I would rate this a 2.5 if it were possible.<br/><br/>I would have liked a bit more character depth and a few less swear words. If this is supposed to be a child's novel is it really okay to say fuck? (most of the time it's fricking and fracking but there is some liberal swearing towards the end). Am I being finicky, is there this much swearing - or elluded swearing - in all children's novels now?<br/><br/>I really enj</span>
  <span id="freeText17299966413629407489" style="display:none">I really wanted to like this novel, and truthfully it wasn't all bad. It just wasn't good either. I would rate this a 2.5 if it were possible.<br /><br />I would have liked a bit more character depth and a few less swear words. If this is supposed to be a child's novel is it really okay to say fuck? (most of the time it's fricking and fracking but there is some liberal swearing towards the end). Am I being finicky, is there this much swearing - or elluded swearing - in all children's novels now?<br /><br />I really enjoyed that Standish had mismatched eyes, they are one of my many krytonites. I knew a boy in elementry school who had one hazel and one blue eye, huge crush, so adorable. I felt cheated a bit though, why did I get no character backstory?!<br /><br />Also, why such short chapters, Gardner? Were 100 chapters within a 278 page book really necessary? And just ewwwww to the rat/maggot/fly sketches, again, Why?! <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Also also, what was up with that ending, Gardner? I knew Standish had to die, breaking into a secret government cover-up and sabotaging it and all, but why the weird present but not concept of death? That rubbed out nonsense was odd.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Gripes, done. <br /><br />There were some good parts to this novel, it was a quick read and it's was imaginative and a bit bizarre - good children's novel concepts - with likable, if not always comprehensible characters. <br /><br />I'm going to bed now, good night <i>Maggot Moon</i>!<br /><br />*Revised note: this is a YA novel? I take back the swear word shots and exchange them for this reads mainly like it's for 8 - 10 year olds not teenagers. </span>

<div id="review_1568833117" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1568833117" />
    <a title="Irshad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/46731504-irshad"><img alt="Irshad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442458915p2/46731504.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1568833117?book_show_action=true">Mar 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Irshad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Irshad" href="/user/show/46731504-irshad">Irshad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781471400445" href="/book/show/17246383-maggot-moon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/46731504-irshad?shelf=excellent-reads">excellent-reads</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1568833117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2555496387797069958"><b>Maggot Moon by Sally Gardner - 3.75/5 stars</b><br/><br/>Maggot Moon is an eerie book that takes place in an alternate historical place pretty much similar to the Nazi days but the main concern here isn't Hitler but the journey to the moon. Standish Treadwell and his Gramps live in Zone Seven where they are outcasts and are from the lower hierarchy chart, they're the unwanted group. They meet a new family, the Lush family, who are coincidentally neighbours and they become the best of friends. Standish and Hec</span>
  <span id="freeText2555496387797069958" style="display:none"><b>Maggot Moon by Sally Gardner - 3.75/5 stars</b><br /><br />Maggot Moon is an eerie book that takes place in an alternate historical place pretty much similar to the Nazi days but the main concern here isn't Hitler but the journey to the moon. Standish Treadwell and his Gramps live in Zone Seven where they are outcasts and are from the lower hierarchy chart, they're the unwanted group. They meet a new family, the Lush family, who are coincidentally neighbours and they become the best of friends. Standish and Hector attend the same school and they defend one another in school bully fights.<br /><br />In this alternate world, the teachers are allowed to punish their students by means of physical violences such as canning, slapping, punching. All that brutal stuff basically. The description of one incident and the loss of Little Eric was rather depressing and plain sad. <br /><i>His eye was popped out from the socket by his teacher just cause he was laughing at his teacher. Apparently the teacher hates looking like a joke.</i><br /><br />It took me awhile to fully comprehend the way the author wrote the plot. It is good after you get into the story. The beginning is rather confusing if you just got out of a reading slump, HAHA!<br /><br />I enjoyed the entire saga that was attempted by Standish to bring down the Motherland for all their hoaxes and deceitful policies. I can't imagine being in such an environment, its just too brutal. People are just taken away if they know too much about the government and are shot if they're unwilling to comply with their rules. Its pure dictatorship that's going on. Horrible. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2555496387797069958" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_630284461" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/630284461" />
    <a title="grdel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8280770-grdel"><img alt="grdel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1394457313p2/8280770.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/630284461?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="grdel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="grdel" href="/user/show/8280770-grdel">grdel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer630284461" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12016606933181266412">I'd heard good things about Maggot Moon, Sally Gardner's 'what if' dystopian fable set in an alternative 1950s Britain under a totalitarian regime. So many good things, in fact, that I saved it for the last of my Carnegie reading, concerned a book described as 'perfect' by none other than Meg Rosoff could not possibly live up to its hype. Reader, it did. I devoured it quickly, over a couple of days which also involved the usual distractions from reading (work, children) and now I want to read it</span>
  <span id="freeText12016606933181266412" style="display:none">I'd heard good things about Maggot Moon, Sally Gardner's 'what if' dystopian fable set in an alternative 1950s Britain under a totalitarian regime. So many good things, in fact, that I saved it for the last of my Carnegie reading, concerned a book described as 'perfect' by none other than Meg Rosoff could not possibly live up to its hype. Reader, it did. I devoured it quickly, over a couple of days which also involved the usual distractions from reading (work, children) and now I want to read it all over again. This is a book one reads with the rising certainty that like How I Live Now or The Book Thief or The Curious Incident... this book will redefine YA literature. Told in brief chapters in first person by Standish Treadwell whose dyslexia is integral to the plot and the means for Gardner to play beautifully with language, there is shocking violence, death, beauty and transcendence in a short, pithy package. The prose is wonderful-there are many gorgeous examples but to quote but one or two:<br /><br />The place smelled of overboiled cabbages, cigarettes and corruption. The teachers had on their glad drags.<br />The striplights looked to me like loneliness. They were too bright, they revealed everything. <br /><br />Read it and weep, aspiring writers. (Sob).<br />As Standish himself says:<br /><br />You see, the what-ifs are as boundless as the stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="12016606933181266412" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2873786576" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2873786576" />
    <a title="Ioana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38614957-ioana"><img alt="Ioana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1518173953p2/38614957.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2873786576?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ioana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ioana" href="/user/show/38614957-ioana">Ioana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2873786576" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15492932037227534186">Guys!! This book was great!! I don't why I waited so long to read it, it had been on my shelf for 6 years I think. But I strongly recommend you to pick this one up. The book covered a lot of my favourite topics such as family, friendship and equality. <br/>The author portrayed so well how it is like to be under the control of a totalitarian regime and how the main character is everything but what this regime is promoting. He is dyslexic and has eyes of different colors, all against their believes bec</span>
  <span id="freeText15492932037227534186" style="display:none">Guys!! This book was great!! I don't why I waited so long to read it, it had been on my shelf for 6 years I think. But I strongly recommend you to pick this one up. The book covered a lot of my favourite topics such as family, friendship and equality. <br />The author portrayed so well how it is like to be under the control of a totalitarian regime and how the main character is everything but what this regime is promoting. He is dyslexic and has eyes of different colors, all against their believes because the government is all about "superior race".<br />The main character, Standish, has a very close relationship with his father because he has been the only one raising him after his parents disappeared. His grandpa doesn't show his emotions very often but you can see just how much he cares about the boy. <br />Apart from his grandfather, Standish makes a new friend, Hector with whom he bonds immediately and develops a beautiful friendship. They dream to escape from their country and live together in a better place. I think this is among my favourite literary friendships because these boys love each other so much and want to protect one another with their lives. <br />Of course, this book doesn't have a happy ending and it is going to break your heart but it deserves to be read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15492932037227534186" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_592858523" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/592858523" />
    <a title="Big Book Little Book" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5702591-big-book-little-book"><img alt="Big Book Little Book" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1342599919p2/5702591.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/592858523?book_show_action=true">Apr 17, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Big Book Little Book" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Big Book Little Book" href="/user/show/5702591-big-book-little-book">Big Book Little Book</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer592858523" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer418521489045863766">Alison for <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.bigbooklittlebook.com'>www.bigbooklittlebook.com</a><br/><br/>Maggot Moon won this year’s Costa Coffee Children’s book Award and is probably the one to beat when it comes to Carnegie. Incredibly original Maggot Moon tells the story of Standish Treadwell, a dyslexic boy, who struggles to read and write, and therefore everybody has decided that he is stupid. The book is set in a dystopian world, but in this case a historical one. The book has the feel of 1950’s Britain, but one that is a totalitarian state of the likes of </span>
  <span id="freeText418521489045863766" style="display:none">Alison for <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bigbooklittlebook.com">www.bigbooklittlebook.com</a><br /><br />Maggot Moon won this year’s Costa Coffee Children’s book Award and is probably the one to beat when it comes to Carnegie. Incredibly original Maggot Moon tells the story of Standish Treadwell, a dyslexic boy, who struggles to read and write, and therefore everybody has decided that he is stupid. The book is set in a dystopian world, but in this case a historical one. The book has the feel of 1950’s Britain, but one that is a totalitarian state of the likes of Hitler’s Germany or Stalinist Russia. The country is now a satellite of the Motherland and every aspect of life is closely monitored.<br /><br />I read this around the time that my daughter was taking the initial screening for dyslexia, which was both a good and a bad thing. It meant that I got distracted by that element of the storyline a little too much, but at the same time was incredibly reassuring. Sally Gardener, the author, is also severely dyslexic and this really shows in how Standish appears to feel about his difficulties with reading and writing. That a dyslexic author has written such an extraordinary book, a book that would be so extraordinary no matter who had written it, really does highlight that dyslexia has absolutely nothing to do with a lack of intelligence and that everybody really can achieve anything, as long as they put their minds to it.<br /><br />It is probably the most heart wrenching book that I have read so far from the shortlist. I defy anybody to have completely dry eyes when they finish the book. The characters of the book are constantly watched; have to guard every word and action, this atmosphere of close oppression just serves to make the emotion feel all the more intense. This is not a book that gives you hope, but then it tells of a world where there is very little hope. It is because of this atmosphere that Standish’s voice is so important. Standish is different, because he thinks outside the box and this is not a regime that is tolerant of differences. That Standish has managed so far is testament to his grandfather. Their relationship highlights the positive side of human nature, in a book that concentrates so heavily on the negative. It highlights the good that people can do even when everything is against them.<br /><br />The writing is just beautiful, whilst at the same time being brutal. The story is told in short chapters, giving the story a stop, start feel that just seems to highlight uncertainty present in the world in which it is set.<br /><br />The short chapters make the book look like it is intended for younger readers, when it probably isn’t. It is a true crossover book in that adults will enjoy it too, but I wouldn’t give it to a child younger than secondary age, the content is quite dark and they wouldn’t necessarily understand some of the complexities of the plot. It is however a book that should be read, not for light hearted enjoyment, but just to experience the incredible writing.<br /><br />Verdict: Beautifully written, if a little brutal at times, a book that just cries out to be read.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="418521489045863766" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_519861996" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/519861996" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5293643-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1374938227p2/5293643.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/519861996?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/5293643-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer519861996" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2469706803868358262">Wow! This grabs you by the collar and pulls you up short and close, whether you like it or not. Standish Treadwell is a dyslexic timid boy with only Hector for a friend and he has disappeared. His world of school and bully boys and headmasters imitates ours to begin with, but soon we realise there is a much darker side. His parents are gone too, there are brick walls and filled-in wells. He lives with Gramps in a street that used to contain "un-bombed houses". The clever words of Standish drip-f</span>
  <span id="freeText2469706803868358262" style="display:none">Wow! This grabs you by the collar and pulls you up short and close, whether you like it or not. Standish Treadwell is a dyslexic timid boy with only Hector for a friend and he has disappeared. His world of school and bully boys and headmasters imitates ours to begin with, but soon we realise there is a much darker side. His parents are gone too, there are brick walls and filled-in wells. He lives with Gramps in a street that used to contain "un-bombed houses". The clever words of Standish drip-feed us with detail of what is occurring - what he, Gramps and the Lushes have acclimatised to, what we have to discover slowly. Many anti- words -" inhuman race" so clever, black humour - all that one can laugh at in this grim violent world. <br /><br />Clever pencil illustration is becoming the vogue in children's literature and here the ominous future awaiting Standish is drawn as flies, rats and later maggots. - buzzing and crawling on and off the pages. <br /><br />The writing is gobsmacking - the boy cannot spell, but uses images and words in a completely original way and with such economy "my heart egg bumping against the side of a pan of boiling water" "that flicking, undone, hangman's rope of a tie" Words are like music to him. And they are - he talks/writes with a rhythm. Sounds, the atmosphere of the coming doom - the readers wades through air as thick as treacle. Standish's words become medicine to Hector in his suffering. standish grows in stature and maturity as he plots to show up the Moon farce - his language grows up too - away from Fricking to fucking. <br /><br />Words v imagination/soul/love. Tongues are cut out as punishment, but actions speak louder than words and minds can hold onto the truth. Fab desc of Gramps' hands like tree roots on p209. Hands that can paint to fool. <br /><br />Stanley succeeds with his mission but of course has no magical powers so the inevitable happens. Desperately sad, but bearable because Hector is there for him and he goes to a safer, brighter place - a place those left behind will now strive to create.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2469706803868358262" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_441796060" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/441796060" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/441796060?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Teresa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Teresa" href="/user/show/402584-teresa">Teresa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781471400049" href="/book/show/14060279-maggot-moon">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer441796060" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4045769281016170100">Our narrator, the wonderfully named Standish Treadwell, is left bereft when his best friend Hector mysteriously disappears, probably taken by the tyrannical goons of the Motherland – a totalitarian regime where dyslexics like Standish are held in scant regard. The Motherland is intent on winning the space race, getting to the moon first without caring who gets hurts in the process. However, what if it was all one big ploy, designed to keep people in their place? What if someone like Standish, so</span>
  <span id="freeText4045769281016170100" style="display:none">Our narrator, the wonderfully named Standish Treadwell, is left bereft when his best friend Hector mysteriously disappears, probably taken by the tyrannical goons of the Motherland – a totalitarian regime where dyslexics like Standish are held in scant regard. The Motherland is intent on winning the space race, getting to the moon first without caring who gets hurts in the process. However, what if it was all one big ploy, designed to keep people in their place? What if someone like Standish, someone perceived to be weak, could debunk the whole scam?<br />As Standish himself remarks<br /><br /> "You see, the what ifs are as boundless as the stars."<br /><br />Equally boundless, it would appear, is Sally Gardner’s wonderful imagination and ability to draw the reader into another world, a parallel universe not that far removed from our own. Using simple language she presents a brutal world, a scary place where folk like Standish are not expected to stand up for themselves. Standish’s neighbourhood, Zone Seven, could be anywhere, any time in history and whilst his day to day life is fraught with danger, he faces the same dilemnas as any teenager – establishing your own identity, forging friendships, learning from your mistakes.<br /><br /><br />Now shortlisted for the Costa Children’s Book Award 2012, Maggot Moon deserves to become a children’s classic. Fans of The Curious Incident of The Dog in the Night-Time, My Sister Lives on the Mantelpiece and Wonder will love this quirky, engaging novel and will perhaps fall a little in love with Standish, your not so average hero. Highly recommended for all ages from 12 upwards.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_618638999" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/618638999?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annie" href="/user/show/4744535-annie">Annie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer618638999" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17002310244330546341">Every description of this book I've read is utterly confusing, and it turns out that it's because it completely defies explanation. I went into this expecting a children's book--the illustrated cover, title, short length all made it seem like a middle school read. But it's honestly one of the darkest and most thought provoking books I've read. <br/><br/>Standish lives in a world that is both completely made up and completely real. (Confession: I tried Googling some of the events in the book after reading </span>
  <span id="freeText17002310244330546341" style="display:none">Every description of this book I've read is utterly confusing, and it turns out that it's because it completely defies explanation. I went into this expecting a children's book--the illustrated cover, title, short length all made it seem like a middle school read. But it's honestly one of the darkest and most thought provoking books I've read. <br /><br />Standish lives in a world that is both completely made up and completely real. (Confession: I tried Googling some of the events in the book after reading it because I was convinced that this must be historical fiction.) It feels at once like a futuristic dystopia and at the same time like historical fiction set in Stalinist Russia or Nazi Germany. His parents were taken; he lives in an annexed and crumbling neighborhood with his grandfather; and behind his house is a giant wall that grows higher by the day. Behind the wall is a mansion that is lit up all day and night despite electricity being an inconsistant rarity for everyone else. It's going across the wall to retrieve a football that sets off a chain of events that slowly unfurls throughout the book.<br /><br />There are so many interesting things about the book that it's impossible to write them all here. You just have to read this. You HAVE TO read this. But I'll tell you a few: 1) There are flip-book-esque illustrations at the bottom of a lot of the pages that are very dark but really interesting in conjunction with the text; 2) The mix of history, science fiction, fantasy, and horror is mesmerizing; 3) Standish is an amazing character and an amazing person.<br /><br />This book takes young adult literature to the next level.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17002310244330546341" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
